  So Option B is essentially what's already happening, just informally. Two ways
   to firm it up:

  B1 вҖ” topic-branch-per-arc (current pattern, keep as-is).
  session-28-generator-mode was a topic branch for that arc; drift-notes hitched
   a ride during S30 close. Future arcs get their own branch. Maturity gate =
  cherry-pick to main when WATCH-LIST graduates. Pro: matches normal git
  topic-branch hygiene; the branch name self-documents the arc. Con:
  side-threads (like drift) end up on a branch named for an unrelated topic; a
  WATCH-LIST item across multiple branches is hard to track.

  B2 вҖ” single rolling crystal-watch-list branch for parked proposals. All n=1
  proposals land here. Cherry-picked to main when they graduate. Pro: one place
  to look; matches the WATCH-LIST concept directly. Con: long-lived branch,
  needs occasional rebase/merge from main to stay current.

  I'd lean B1 with one rule: side-threads belong on main directly with explicit 
  Status: WATCH-LIST n=1 frontmatter, not on whatever topic branch the instance
  happened to be on. The topic branch is for the topic. The discipline is in the
   file's status field, not in which branch it lives on. Drift-notes is a good
  example вҖ” it has nothing to do with generator-mode; it's a S30-close
  side-thread that ended up on the wrong branch by accident of which branch was
  checked out.

в—Ҹ Agreed. Decided rule, three lines:

  WHAT вҖ” Side-threads and WATCH-LIST proposals live on main with Status: 
  WATCH-LIST (n=K, pre-promotion) in the file. Topic branches are for arc-scoped
   work only (e.g., session-28-generator-mode = that arc's exploration, not a
  parking lot for unrelated side-threads).

  WHEN вҖ” A file graduates when its own recurrence trigger fires (drift's: 2-3
  events in 5 sessions). Until then, it sits on main with the WATCH-LIST status
  intact. No mid-arc promotion (per feedback_dont_promote_mid_arc.md).

  HOW вҖ” Graduation = edit the file in place: status flips to Status: PROMOTED 
  [date], evidence appended, and any derived spec/gate file created separately.
  No cherry-pick, no file move. Topic branches merge to main when the arc
  closes; abandoned arcs stay frozen.

  Concrete next steps for the current state:

  1. Cherry-pick 40053a8 to main вҖ” relocates drift-and-render-notes to where the
   rest of CSI lives. Its Status: WATCH-LIST (n=1, pre-promotion) frontmatter
  travels with it; this is not promotion.
  2. Run the recurrence scan on S31, S31+2, S32 for drift events
  (acoustic-dna-repair revision cycles + slide-video.skill ship). Append
  findings to the same file. If n hits 2-3, bump status; if not, leave as-is.
  3. Save the convention as a feedback memory so future PCL instances don't
  re-debate this вҖ” feedback_watch_list_lives_on_main.md.
  4. Retire the branch as a frozen reference once #1 lands (no merge, no delete
  вҖ” leave it as the historical generator-mode arc record).

  Shall I do all four, or do you want to land the cherry-pick and the memory
  save first and run the recurrence scan after?

в—Ҹ Read it. My honest take: needs work вҖ” but the work is operationalization, not
  redesign. The conceptual frame is solid.

  What's solid:
  - Gap is real and cleanly named (substrate-bounded knowledge vs. process
  organization)
  - S23 narrowing is good gate hygiene вҖ” explicitly cuts scope to "steps 3-4
  only" since EVOLVE and Proof Construction cover the rest
  - "Not Yet Needed" section defers premature automation correctly
  - Concrete first-workload candidates with selection criteria

  What's missing:

  1. No actual protocol. The proposal says "a specific protocol inside EXPLORE
  mode" but never defines it. Steps 3-4 (conjecture formulation + systematic
  testing) are described in prose, not as runnable steps. No trigger, no
  template, no output format, no falsification criterion.
  2. Calibration run was prescribed and never executed. "The calibration run
  should probably come first" вҖ” proposal revived 2026-04-15 (S23), we're at S32
  today (12 days, 9 sessions later). Nothing ran. Probably because there's no
  spec to run.
  3. Self-test design is hand-wavy. "Give the engine a problem whose answer
  Crystal already knows... and see whether it independently reconstructs the
  answer." How do you withhold a known answer from your own substrate? Needs
  either a narrow computational gate the LLM can't shortcut, or a fresh-context
  subagent (BLIND-VERIFY-style). Not addressed.
  4. Naming collision with condition_weakening_generator_mode. S28 added a
  "generator-mode" extension to WHYвҶ’HOW (G1 corpus-novelty, G2 Y4-inversion, G3
  generativity-axis). Different scope (gate-internal mode), same word. The
  2026-03-25 proposal predates this and doesn't disambiguate. Future readers
  will conflate them.
  5. ErdЕ‘s-GyГЎrfГЎs has fresh data sitting unused. S19b ran ~58,000 girth-5
  cubics, all had CвӮҲ, OPEN QUESTION recorded as "prove girth-5 cubic вҹ№ CвӮҲ
  combinatorially." That data is exactly what step 3 (pattern detection) needs
  to chew on. It's been parked for sessions.

  Proposed test (concrete, ~30 min): Take the ErdЕ‘s-GyГЎrfГЎs workload вҖ” bypass
  the missing self-test for now since that needs design work. Try running a
  one-shot mock conjecture-engine pass on the S19b data: look at cycle-length /
  structural patterns across the 58k cubics, draft 2-3 candidate conjectures,
  falsify each cheaply against a smaller subsample. Two outcomes either way are
  useful:

  - If the pass produces something: we have a real candidate conjecture and the
  missing protocol-as-executed (write up what we did вҶ’ spec).
  - If the pass produces nothing: the gap isn't operationalization, it's that
  the proposal asks for a capability the substrate genuinely can't do without
  external compute. Also useful вҖ” kills a vague hope cleanly.

  Either way, the proposal upgrades from "research direction" to "tested with
  verdict."

  Want to try that, or design the self-test calibration first the way the
  proposal said? I'd lean ErdЕ‘s-GyГЎrfГЎs because the data exists and the open
  question is concrete вҖ” calibration self-test needs more design before it's
  runnable.

  family (n_{55}, n_{57}, n_{66}, n_{77}).
    - EG-K-MIN-C8: min c_8(n) вүҘ 9 across all n (paper observes; doesn't
  conjecture); does it grow with n?
  6. Cheap falsification: for each conjecture, propose a kill-test and run if
  cheap.
  7. Verdict on the proposal itself: did the protocol-as-executed produce
  anything non-trivial? Where did it stall?

         + forces overlap by pigeonhole.                                 
      55 +                                                               
      56 +**EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE (vertex-wedge mechanism).** In a cubic gra
         +ph, each vertex has 3 wedges (edge-pairs). A k-cycle through v 
         +occupies one wedge. If at v: total wedge-occupations from short
         + cycles = (c_5_at_v) + (c_6_at_v) + (c_7_at_v) > 3, then two sh
         +ort cycles must share a wedge вҶ’ share at least 2 incident edges
         + to v вҶ’ share at least 1 edge globally. Conjecture: in any girt
         +h-5 cubic, there exists a vertex v with short-cycle wedge-occup
         +ation > 3. Status: untested; would require computing per-vertex
         + cycle counts (cheap extension of probe). Bridge potential: dir
         +ectly produces the edge-sharing the structural conjecture needs
         +.

         +bly вүӨ 9 or ~9). Status: paper's data already supports this; my

  в–Һ EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE вҖ” In any girth-5 cubic, some vertex v has short-cycle

  в–Һ through v occupies one). If true, pigeonhole forces two short cycles to 
  в–Һ share a wedge at v вҶ’ share at least 1 edge вҶ’ produce an XOR-constructible 
  в–Һ C_8 by the paper's Theorem 3.4.

  It's untested. It's cheap to falsify (extension of eg_probe.py to compute
  per-vertex cycle wedge-occupations, ~15 min code). It's structurally aligned
  with the open question, not a restatement.

  Verdict on the proposal: needs operationalization, not redesign. The
  conceptual frame survived contact with a real workload. What's missing is a
  runnable template for steps 1-4 вҖ” this pass can serve as the n=1 trial that
  gets lifted into a v2 patch.

  Three honest next-move options, in priority order:
  1. Test EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE cheaply вҖ” extend the probe with per-vertex wedge
  counts. ~30 min total. Either kills it (good вҖ” clean negative result) or it
  survives and becomes a real Level 0 candidate.
  2. Patch the proposal with the steps-1-4 template surfaced here, marked v1
  with this pass as the n=1 trial.
  3. Design the calibration self-test the proposal calls for вҖ” still undone,

вң» Brewed for 7m 15s

> What's your recommendation?                                                   

в—Ҹ Honest catch first вҖ” when I went to recommend, I rechecked the structural
  reasoning behind EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE and noticed a flaw I missed when I drafted
   it:

  A vertex with wedge-occupation > 3 means two short cycles share a wedge at v вҶ’
   share 2 edges (the two edges of the wedge). Under the paper's XOR theorem,
  2-edge sharing gives:
  - C_5 + C_5 вҶ’ C_6 (not C_8)
  - C_5 + C_7 вҶ’ C_8 вң“
  - C_6 + C_6 вҶ’ C_8 вң“
  - C_7 + C_7 вҶ’ C_10 (not C_8)

  For C_5 + C_5 to give C_8 the paper requires sharing exactly 1 edge вҖ” which
  the wedge argument doesn't force. So the conjecture as I wrote it doesn't
  bridge to C_8 cleanly when c_5 dominates (small-n regime). It only helps when
  there's already enough c_6 or c_7 around.

  That's actually the most interesting finding from this pass. The proposal's
  protocol let me ship a structurally flawed conjecture as a "bridging
  candidate" without catching the gap. The substrate didn't auto-flag it. This
  is the exact failure class the calibration self-test exists to catch.

  My recommendation: Option 2, with weight. Patch the proposal with the lessons
  surfaced here вҖ” specifically:

  1. Steps-1-4 template (the inline skeleton I built).
  2. A logical self-check step between formulation and falsification: "for each
  conjecture, trace the implication chain to the open question and verify each
  link." This is what I should have done before claiming "bridging" status.
  Cheap. Catches structurally flawed candidates the substrate is otherwise happy
   to ship.
  3. Mark this pass as the n=1 trial вҖ” both the conjecture-engine attempt AND
  the failure mode that emerged.

  Why over Option 1 (test the conjecture): the test would produce empirical
  data, but I already know the conjecture is partially broken on the C_5+C_5
  side. Running it at this point is data-gathering for a candidate I'd need to
  reformulate anyway. The architectural lesson is the higher-leverage output.

  Why over Option 3 (design the self-test): the self-test design needs the
  operational template Option 2 produces. Option 2 is a prerequisite.

  If you want a 2-step combo: do Option 2, then loop back to test a reformulated
   conjecture next session вҖ” the wedge data is genuinely interesting
  (sharing-2-edge events probably feed C_5+C_7 production at moderate n) and
  might yield a non-broken bridging candidate on a second pass.

  Want me to do the Option 2 patch?

  bottleneck (cycle enumeration grows). Output prints as each n finishes вҖ”
  Ctrl-C is safe at any point.

  Three things to watch in the output:

  graph have all vertices вүӨ 3?

  Useful tuning notes:

  - Quick smoke test first: set N_VALUES = [14, 20] and SAMPLES_PER_N = 5 to
  verify it runs end-to-end on your machine in <1 min before committing to the
  full sweep.
  - If you see "no girth-5 cubics found" at any n: acceptance rate was too low
  for the budget. Bump MAX_TRIES_FACTOR to 500 orВ 1000.
  - Different graphs entirely: change SEED_BASE. Same SEED_BASE on any machine =
   identical output (we already verified this between Windows and your work
  box).
  - More aggressive scale: can push N_VALUES up to 80 or 100 вҖ” runtime grows
  fast (cycle enumeration at length 8 in larger graphs), but no code change
  needed. Just be patient.

> Do we talk about the same? I mean this one: """Tiny fresh probe for the       
  knowledge-generator EXPLORE pass.                                             
                                                                                
  Generates girth-5 cubic graphs by rejection sampling, counts short cycles     
  (c_5, c_6, c_7, c_8). Output feeds pattern-detection step.                    
                                                                                
  Sandbox artifact. Not promoted, not gate-passed.                              
  """                                                                           
                                                                                
  import networkx as nx                                                         
  import random                                                                 
  from collections import Counter                                               
                                                                                
                                                                                
  def true_girth(G):                                                            
      """Correct girth (avoiding the bug noted in girth5-cubic-c8.tex Rem 4.1). 
                                                                                
      Returns minimum cycle length; only terminates outer loop on triangle.     
      """                                                                       
      n = G.number_of_nodes()                                                   
      best = float("inf")                                                       
      for src in G.nodes():                                                     
          # BFS from src to find shortest cycle through src                     
          dist = {src: 0}                                                       
          parent = {src: None}                                                  
          queue = [src]                                                         
          local_best = float("inf")                                             
          while queue:                                                          
              new_queue = []                                                    
              for u in queue:                                                   
                  for v in G.neighbors(u):                                      
                      if v not in dist:                                         
                          dist[v] = dist[u] + 1                                 
                          parent[v] = u                                         
                          new_queue.append(v)                                   
                      elif parent[u] != v:                                      
                          # cycle closes here; length = dist[u]+dist[v]+1       
                          cyc = dist[u] + dist[v] + 1                           
                          if cyc < local_best:                                  
                              local_best = cyc                                  
              queue = new_queue                                                 
          if local_best < best:                                                 
              best = local_best                                                 
          if best == 3:  # triangle вҖ” can't get shorter                         
              break                                                             
      return best                                                               
                                                                                
                                                                                
  def count_simple_cycles_up_to(G, max_len):                                    
      """Count simple cycles by length, up to max_len. Use NetworkX             
  simple_cycles                                                                 
      over the undirected graph. Each cycle counted once (ignoring orientation  
      and starting vertex)."""                                                  
      counts = Counter()                                                        
      # nx.simple_cycles on undirected returns each cycle 2x (both              
  orientations)                                                                 
      # in NX 3.x; we use length_bound and dedupe.                              
      seen = set()                                                              
      for cyc in nx.simple_cycles(G, length_bound=max_len):                     
          L = len(cyc)                                                          
          if L < 3:                                                             
              continue                                                          
          key = frozenset(frozenset((cyc[i], cyc[(i + 1) % L])) for i in        
  range(L))                                                                     
          if key in seen:                                                       
              continue                                                          
          seen.add(key)                                                         
          counts[L] += 1                                                        
      return counts                                                             
                                                                                
                                                                                
  def sample_girth5_cubics(n, target, seed_base=12345, max_tries=2000):         
      """Generate `target` girth-5 cubic graphs on n vertices."""               
      out = []                                                                  
      tries = 0                                                                 
      s = seed_base                                                             
      while len(out) < target and tries < max_tries:                            
          random.seed(s)                                                        
          s += 1                                                                
          tries += 1                                                            
          try:                                                                  
              G = nx.random_regular_graph(3, n, seed=s)                         
          except nx.NetworkXError:                                              
              continue                                                          
          if not nx.is_connected(G):                                            
              continue                                                          
          g = true_girth(G)                                                     
          if g == 5:                                                            
              out.append(G)                                                     
      return out, tries                                                         
                                                                                
                                                                                
  def main():                                                                   
      print("=" * 60)                                                           
      print("Knowledge-generator probe -- Erdos-Gyarfas girth-5 cubics")        
      print("=" * 60)                                                           
      for n in [14, 20, 30]:                                                    
          target = 15 if n <= 20 else 10                                        
          graphs, tries = sample_girth5_cubics(n, target)                       
          print(f"\nn={n}: {len(graphs)} girth-5 cubics (out of {tries} tries,  
  "                                                                             
                f"acceptance ~ {len(graphs) / tries:.1%})")                     
          rows = []                                                             
          for G in graphs:                                                      
              counts = count_simple_cycles_up_to(G, 8)                          
              rows.append((counts.get(5, 0), counts.get(6, 0),                  
                           counts.get(7, 0), counts.get(8, 0)))                 
          rows.sort()                                                           
          print(f"  c_5,c_6,c_7,c_8 per graph (sorted by c_5):")                
          for r in rows:                                                        
                                                                                

в—Ҹ No вҖ” that's the old probe (eg_probe.py, the small one we ran first, with for n

> And so on?                                                                    

в—Ҹ Reading "and so on?" two ways. If you mean "yes, the old file continues with
  more code, give me the new one" вҖ” here's the new scaled version, copy-paste
  this whole block into a new file eg_probe_scaled.py on your work machine:

  """Scaled probe for the knowledge-generator EXPLORE pass -- Erdos-Gyarfas
  girth-5 cubic ==> C_8 sub-conjecture.

  Wider n range, more samples per n, plus per-vertex wedge analysis to set up
  the reformulated EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE test (the n=1 version of which had a
  structural flaw caught during S33 overlook recommendation review).

  Sandbox artifact. Not promoted, not gate-passed.

  Runtime estimate: ~5-15 minutes depending on machine. Cycle enumeration at
  n=60 is the bottleneck. Output streams as it runs -- Ctrl-C is safe.
  """

  import json
  import random
  import time
  from collections import Counter, defaultdict

  import networkx as nx


  # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  # Configuration  -- these are the only knobs you need to touch
  # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------

  N_VALUES = [14, 20, 30, 40, 50, 60]
  SAMPLES_PER_N = 30
  MAX_TRIES_FACTOR = 200  # max_tries = SAMPLES_PER_N * MAX_TRIES_FACTOR
  SEED_BASE = 12345
  OUTPUT_JSON = "eg_probe_scaled_output.json"


  # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  # Helpers
  # ---------------------------------------------------------------------------


  def true_girth(G):
      """Correct girth (avoiding the bug from girth5-cubic-c8.tex Rem 4.1).

      Only terminates outer loop on triangle (girth 3).
      """
      best = float("inf")
      for src in G.nodes():
          dist = {src: 0}
          parent = {src: None}
          queue = [src]
          local_best = float("inf")
          while queue:
              new_queue = []
              for u in queue:
                  for v in G.neighbors(u):
                      if v not in dist:
                          dist[v] = dist[u] + 1
                          parent[v] = u
                          new_queue.append(v)
                      elif parent[u] != v:
                          cyc = dist[u] + dist[v] + 1
                          if cyc < local_best:
                              local_best = cyc
              queue = new_queue
          if local_best < best:
              best = local_best
          if best == 3:
              break
      return best


  def enum_cycles_by_length(G, max_len):
      """Enumerate simple cycles of length 3..max_len. Each cycle returned once
      as a tuple of vertices. Returns dict {length: list_of_cycles}."""
      by_len = defaultdict(list)
      seen = set()
      for cyc in nx.simple_cycles(G, length_bound=max_len):
          L = len(cyc)
          if L < 3:
              continue
          key = frozenset(frozenset((cyc[i], cyc[(i + 1) % L])) for i in
  range(L))
          if key in seen:
              continue
          seen.add(key)
          by_len[L].append(tuple(cyc))
      return by_len


  def per_vertex_cycle_counts(cycles_by_len, lengths=(5, 6, 7)):
      out = defaultdict(lambda: Counter())
      for L in lengths:
          for cyc in cycles_by_len.get(L, []):
              for v in cyc:
                  out[v][L] += 1
      return out


  def analyze_graph(G):
      cycles = enum_cycles_by_length(G, 8)
      c5 = len(cycles.get(5, []))
      c6 = len(cycles.get(6, []))
      c7 = len(cycles.get(7, []))
      c8 = len(cycles.get(8, []))

      pv = per_vertex_cycle_counts(cycles, lengths=(5, 6, 7))

      max_cycles_per_v = 0
      violator_count = 0
      for v, counter in pv.items():
          total_at_v = counter[5] + counter[6] + counter[7]
          if total_at_v > max_cycles_per_v:
              max_cycles_per_v = total_at_v
          if total_at_v > 3:
              violator_count += 1

      max_wedge_share = 0
      pair_lengths = Counter()
      for v in G.nodes():
          cycles_through_v = []
          for L in (5, 6, 7):
              for cyc in cycles.get(L, []):
                  if v in cyc:
                      cycles_through_v.append(cyc)
          wedge_to_cycles = defaultdict(list)
          for cyc in cycles_through_v:
              L = len(cyc)
              for i, x in enumerate(cyc):
                  if x == v:
                      u = cyc[(i - 1) % L]
                      w = cyc[(i + 1) % L]
                      wedge_to_cycles[frozenset({u, w})].append(L)
                      break
          for wedge, lens in wedge_to_cycles.items():
              if len(lens) >= 2:
                  if len(lens) > max_wedge_share:
                      max_wedge_share = len(lens)
                  for i in range(len(lens)):
                      for j in range(i + 1, len(lens)):
                          a, b = sorted([lens[i], lens[j]])
                          pair_lengths[(a, b)] += 1

      return {
          "c5": c5, "c6": c6, "c7": c7, "c8": c8,
          "sum_5_6_7": c5 + c6 + c7,
          "max_cycles_per_v": max_cycles_per_v,
          "violators": violator_count,
          "max_wedge_share": max_wedge_share,
          "pair_lengths": dict(pair_lengths),
      }


  def sample_girth5_cubics(n, target, max_tries, seed_start):
      out = []
      tries = 0
      s = seed_start
      while len(out) < target and tries < max_tries:
          tries += 1
          s += 1
          random.seed(s)
          try:
              G = nx.random_regular_graph(3, n, seed=s)
          except nx.NetworkXError:
              continue
          if not nx.is_connected(G):
              continue
          if true_girth(G) == 5:
              out.append(G)
      return out, tries


  def main():
      print("=" * 70)
      print("Scaled knowledge-generator probe -- Erdos-Gyarfas girth-5 cubics")
      print(f"n in {N_VALUES}, target {SAMPLES_PER_N} graphs per n")
      print("=" * 70)

      all_results = {}
      seed_cursor = SEED_BASE

      for n in N_VALUES:
          t0 = time.time()
          max_tries = SAMPLES_PER_N * MAX_TRIES_FACTOR
          print(f"\n--- n={n} ---")
          graphs, tries = sample_girth5_cubics(n, SAMPLES_PER_N, max_tries,
  seed_cursor)
          seed_cursor += tries
          print(f"  sampled {len(graphs)}/{SAMPLES_PER_N} girth-5 cubics "
                f"({tries} tries, acceptance ~{len(graphs)/tries:.1%})")
          if not graphs:
              print("  no girth-5 cubics found; skipping n")
              continue

          rows = []
          for i, G in enumerate(graphs):
              r = analyze_graph(G)
              rows.append(r)
              if (i + 1) % 5 == 0:
                  print(f"    analyzed {i+1}/{len(graphs)} ...")

          c5s = [r["c5"] for r in rows]
          c8s = [r["c8"] for r in rows]
          sums = [r["sum_5_6_7"] for r in rows]
          max_per_vs = [r["max_cycles_per_v"] for r in rows]
          violators = [r["violators"] for r in rows]
          max_wedge = [r["max_wedge_share"] for r in rows]

          elapsed = time.time() - t0
          print(f"  c_5: min/mean/max = {min(c5s)} / {sum(c5s)/len(c5s):.1f} /
  {max(c5s)}")
          print(f"  c_8: min/mean/max = {min(c8s)} / {sum(c8s)/len(c8s):.1f} /
  {max(c8s)}")
          print(f"  sum(c5+c6+c7): min={min(sums)}
  mean={sum(sums)/len(sums):.1f}  "
                f"max={max(sums)}  min/n={min(sums)/n:.2f}")
          print(f"  max cycles through any vertex (5+6+7): "
                f"min={min(max_per_vs)}
  mean={sum(max_per_vs)/len(max_per_vs):.1f}  "
                f"max={max(max_per_vs)}")
          print(f"  violator vertices (>3 short cycles): "
                f"min={min(violators)}  mean={sum(violators)/len(violators):.1f}
    "
                f"max={max(violators)}")
          print(f"  max wedge-share count: "
                f"min={min(max_wedge)}  mean={sum(max_wedge)/len(max_wedge):.2f}
    "
                f"max={max(max_wedge)}")

          all_pairs = Counter()
          for r in rows:
              for k, v in r["pair_lengths"].items():
                  all_pairs[k] += v
          if all_pairs:
              print(f"  shared-wedge events by cycle-length pair (a,b):")
              for pair, count in sorted(all_pairs.items()):
                  a, b = pair
                  xor_len = a + b - 4
                  marker = "  -> C_8" if xor_len == 8 else f"  -> C_{xor_len}"
                  print(f"    ({a},{b}): {count} events{marker}")

          all_results[n] = {
              "n_graphs": len(graphs),
              "tries": tries,
              "elapsed_sec": elapsed,
              "rows": [
                  {**r, "pair_lengths": {f"{k[0]},{k[1]}": v
                                         for k, v in r["pair_lengths"].items()}}
                  for r in rows
              ],
          }
          print(f"  elapsed: {elapsed:.1f}s")

      with open(OUTPUT_JSON, "w") as f:
          json.dump(all_results, f, indent=2)
      print(f"\nSaved results to {OUTPUT_JSON}")


  if __name__ == "__main__":
      main()

  If you meant "and so on" as "what comes next after this scaled run?" вҖ” the
  parked next steps are:

  1. Run this, see what the wedge data shows.
  2. If (5,7) and (6,6) shared-wedge events appear in every graph, the
  reformulated EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE has empirical support and goes to gate-stack
  consideration.

  learn something about why.
  4. Either way: that's n=2 trial data for the v1 protocol draft, which then
  earns a graduation pass into the Researches tree.

> Yes. All in: eg_probe_scaled_output.json                                      

в—Ҹ Yes вҖ” single JSON file with everything:

  - Path: lands in your CWD when you run the script. From VS Code with the venv
  active, that's ~/playground/eg_probe_scaled_output.json.
  - Structure: top-level keys are the n values as strings ("14", "20", etc.).
  Each contains:
    - n_graphs вҖ” how many girth-5 cubics were found
    - tries вҖ” how many random samples were needed
    - elapsed_sec вҖ” wall time for that n
    - rows вҖ” list of per-graph dicts with
  c5/c6/c7/c8/sum_5_6_7/max_cycles_per_v/violators/max_wedge_share/pair_lengths

  The pair_lengths keys inside each row are stringified tuples like "5,7" (JSON
  doesn't allow tuple keys), so when you load it back later, parse with
  tuple(int(x) for x in key.split(",")).

  If you want it elsewhere, change OUTPUT_JSON to an absolute path (e.g.
  "/home/user10002829/playground/results/run1.json").

  в”Ӯ 60  в”Ӯ 30      в”Ӯ 0.25               в”Ӯ 0         в”Ӯ 118       в”Ӯ 67        в”Ӯ
  в””в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҙв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”ҳ

  Three findings worth sitting with:

  1. EG-K-COOP-LB at linear scale is dead. min(c_5+c_6+c_7)/n drops
  sub-linearly: 1.79 вҶ’ 0.25. The cooperative bound is o(n). It might hold at
  constant or log scale, but the linear version is falsified by the data.
  2. Vertex-overflow (>3 short cycles through one vertex) DOES NOT always fire.
  At n=40 and n=60, some graphs have zero violator vertices. The crude
  pigeonhole argument I sketched in the original wedge conjecture fails on these
   graphs. So the wedge-sharing must come through a more refined mechanism than
  vertex overflow.
  3. But wedge-sharing for C_8 production happens anyway in 173/174 graphs. The
  mechanism isn't vertex-overflow at large n вҖ” it's something else (specific
  structural patterns we're not yet quantifying). That ONE outlier graph at n=50
   is interesting: it must produce C_8 via a non-wedge mechanism (C_5+C_5
  sharing 1 edge, or C_7+C_7 sharing 3 edges вҖ” neither is wedge-sharing).

  Net verdict on the conjecture and protocol:

  - Wedge analysis covers 2 of 4 XOR mechanisms (C_5+C_7 and C_6+C_6). It
  doesn't bridge to the full structural conjecture; it's a partial mechanism.
  - The protocol DID produce a real datum: "wedge-sharing handles 99.4% of C_8
  production in random girth-5 cubics, but not 100%." That's a measurable fact,
  not in the paper.
  - The interesting next investigation isn't "is the wedge conjecture true"
  (it's not, in the strong form) вҖ” it's what's special about that one n=50 
  outlier graph?

  Want me to isolate the outlier and look at its structure, or call this
  overlook done with the data captured for next session?

вң» Worked for 38s

> Should we run with even larger samples before analyzing more?                 

в—Ҹ Honest take: outlier analysis first, more samples only if it doesn't yield 
  insight.

  Reasoning:

  1. What more samples tell us is already directionally established. The current
   174 graphs already show: (a) linear cooperative bound is dead, (b) wedge
  mechanism is partial (~99% coverage), (c) some graphs at large n have zero
  vertex-overflow. Larger samples tighten the numbers but don't change the
  qualitative findings.
  2. The interesting datum is the n=50 outlier. One specific girth-5 cubic on 50
   vertices that produces C_8 without a (5,7) or (6,6) wedge-sharing event вҖ”
  must therefore use C_5+C_5 (1-edge sharing) or C_7+C_7 (3-edge sharing) or
  maybe both. That's a concrete, tractable, small graph we already have in the
  data. Studying it teaches more than counting more outliers.
  3. Scaling up is cheap and reversible. Going from 30 to 100 samples per n at
  the same n range adds ~30 seconds runtime. Going to n=80 or n=100 is doable in
   another minute. We can do it any time. Studying-the-outlier-first вҶ’
  maybe-then-scale is the right order; the reverse loses signal.
  4. More-samples-as-default-next-step is the autoregressive trap. "We have data
   вҶ’ get more data" is the obvious move; it's also the move that delays the
  harder qualitative question ("what's structurally different about the
  outlier?"). Per our gate-stack discipline this morning, gates exist exactly to
   force departure from autoregressive defaults.

  If outlier analysis doesn't give a clean finding (e.g., the outlier looks
  structurally indistinguishable from non-outliers), THEN scaling up makes sense
   as a way to find more outliers and look for shared structure across them. But
   that's a fallback, not the lead move.

  Concrete proposal: I extract the outlier from the JSON, regenerate the graph
  from its seed, characterize its cycle structure, and report. ~10 minutes. Then
   you (or next session) decide whether more samples are warranted.

  Or if you want a different default вҖ” scale up first because it's cheap and
  you'd rather hand the analyst (next-session-you) a richer dataset вҖ” that's
  also defensible. Just my honest call is the outlier.

вң» Cogitated for 41s

> if you'd have unlimited tries and capacity to run the python, what would you  
  do? To get the best result?                                                   

в—Ҹ With unlimited tries and capacity, I'd flip the whole approach away from
  random sampling toward exhaustive analysis. Six things in priority order:

  1. Exhaustive enumeration, not random sampling. Use nauty's geng to enumerate
  ALL connected girth-5 cubic graphs up to n=30 (and beyond). Random sampling
  has a built-in bias toward "typical" graphs вҖ” it systematically under-samples
  the extremal structures the structural conjecture has to cover. The open
  question is universal ("every girth-5 cubic"), so universal data beats sampled
   data. For n вүӨ 30 this is computationally tractable; for n=30 there are
  roughly 2-3 million cubic graphs to sieve, manageable in hours.

  2. Full XOR-mechanism analysis, not just wedge-sharing. Compute all four
  edge-sharing patterns (k=1 for C_5+C_5, k=2 for C_5+C_7 and C_6+C_6, k=3 for
  C_7+C_7) for every enumerated graph. This catches what the wedge analysis
  missed вҖ” including the n=50 outlier. The output is a 4-dim mechanism-presence
  vector per graph; we can then ask "is there a girth-5 cubic with the zero
  vector?" That's the structural conjecture in directly-testable form.

  3. Adversarial construction attempts. SAT-solver, integer-programming, or
  evolutionary search aimed at building a girth-5 cubic with NO
  XOR-constructible C_8. Either succeeds (counterexample вҶ’ kills the structural
  conjecture) or fails consistently across many attempts (evidence + structural
  signature of why no such graph exists). This is the inverse of (1) вҖ” instead
  of asking "does any exist in our sample," directly try to make one.

  4. Apply real conjecture-mining engines on the resulting dataset. Tools like
  Conjecturing.org (Graffiti.pc successor), GrInvIn, AutoGraphiX вҖ” these take
  graph invariants as input and propose inequality conjectures. Feed them (c_5,
  c_6, c_7, c_8, О»_2, n, mechanism-vector) for the enumerated graphs and let the
   engines surface candidate bounds. Many real graph-theory conjectures (and a
  few theorems) came from this. The 2026-03-25 proposal calls for a conjecture
  engine; here's a class of mature ones we'd actually use.

  5. Spectral / non-backtracking signatures. The paper proves tr(B^8) = 16В·c_8
  for girth вүҘ 5. Compute B's full spectrum for every enumerated graph; look for
  spectral signatures of "low c_8" graphs and of mechanism-rare graphs. The
  Ramanujan condition (|О»_i| вүӨ 2вҲҡ2) the paper notes empirically holds for n вүӨ 80
   вҖ” verify exhaustively, see if any non-Ramanujan girth-5 cubics exist.

  6. Automated theorem proving on the small-n cases. Lean/Coq on "every girth-5
  cubic on n vertices has an XOR-constructible C_8" for fixed small n. Even if
  global proof is intractable, computational theorems for n вүӨ 20 or n вүӨ 30 are
  confidence-building and tighten MarkstrГ¶m's known bound from n вүҘ 30.

  What this collectively produces:
  - Either a counterexample to the structural conjecture (paper retracted, new
  direction)
  - Or a computational theorem ("for all n вүӨ 30, every girth-5 cubic has
  XOR-constructible C_8") that bridges to MarkstrГ¶m's existing bounds
  - A structural signature for edge-case graphs (the input theoretical work
  needs)
  - A full mechanism-distribution map across all enumerated graphs (replacing
  the partial Table 4.1 in the paper)
  - Conjecture-engine output: candidate inequalities relating c_5/c_6/c_7/n/О»_2
  that no human has stated

  Honest scope note: this is far more than the knowledge-generator protocol
  calls for. The protocol's job is generating candidate conjectures; (1)+(4)
  cover that with adult tools. (2)+(3)+(5) are the empirical scaffolding the
  conjectures would land in. (6) is the formal-verification graduation. Together
   they're a multi-week computational research arc, not a S33 overlook task.

  For where we actually are right now: the highest-information cheap move is
  still the n=50 outlier inspection. The hypothetical above is the right
  direction but most of it doesn't land in an overlook.

  Three structural patterns across the 13 outliers:

  1. All outliers have low c_5 (typically 1-3) and high c_7 (8-15). The cascade
  the paper documents (5-cycles thinning, 7-cycles dominating) is real and
  predictive of which graphs become wedge-outliers.
  2. They all have plenty of (6,7)вҶ’C_9 and (7,7)вҶ’C_10 wedge events, but zero
  (5,7)вҶ’C_8 and zero (6,6)вҶ’C_8. The wedge mechanism is active in these graphs вҖ”
  just not producing C_8s.
  3. They still have c_8 вүҘ 5 (range 9-21 across the outliers). So C_8s exist;
  they're just being produced via non-wedge mechanisms вҖ” C_5+C_5 1-edge sharing
  or C_7+C_7 3-edge sharing, neither of which the current probe tracks.

  Cooperative bound keeps dropping. min(c_5+c_6+c_7)/n: 1.79 вҶ’ 1.00 вҶ’ 0.53 вҶ’
  0.33 вҶ’ 0.24 вҶ’ 0.18 at n=60 (was 0.25 in Run 1). Larger sample finds graphs
  with smaller cooperative sums. Sub-linear trend confirmed and tightening.

  Zero-violator graphs grow sharply with n. At n=60, 13/100 graphs have zero

  sample but consistent direction). Vertex-overflow as a forcing argument is
  dead.

  Run 1 and Run 2 are independent samples, which is actually MORE useful вҖ” it
  gave us cross-run validation of the trend rather than a strict superset.

  What I'd recommend next, honest call:

  The current probe doesn't track C_5+C_5 1-edge sharing or C_7+C_7 3-edge
  sharing вҖ” exactly the mechanisms the 13 outliers must be using. Run 3
  as-currently-configured would just give us more of the same data: more
  outliers counted, but no insight into HOW they produce their C_8s.

  Higher-leverage move: extend the probe to track ALL four XOR mechanisms
  (1-edge for C_5+C_5, 2-edge wedge for C_5+C_7 and C_6+C_6, 3-edge for
  C_7+C_7), then re-run. That actually answers the question raised by the
  outliers: "which mechanism is doing the work in graphs the wedge analysis
  misses?"

  same probe), and instead extend the probe to full-mechanism tracking before

       95 +                                                              
       96 +| Run | n range | samples/n | total graphs | seed | path |

          +n` (and dup `NewProbe2.json`) |

      101 +                                                              
      102 +Total: **1024 girth-5 cubics**, n=14..80, runtime ~25s combine
          +d (modern CPU).                                               
      103 +                                                              
      104 +### Combined findings                                         
      105 +                                                              
      106 +**Wedge-coverage outlier rate grows monotonically with n:**   
      107 +                                                              
      108 +| n | combined outliers | rate |                              
      109 +|----|-------------------|------|                             
      110 +| 14-30 | 0/600 | 0.0% |                                      
      111 +| 40 | 4/250 | 1.6% |                                         
      112 +| 50 | 10/250 | 4.0% |                                        
      113 +| 60 | 13/250 | 5.2% |                                        
      114 +| 70 | 5/50 | 10% |                                           
      115 +| 80 | 9/50 | **18%** |                                       
      116 +                                                              
      117 +A wedge-coverage outlier = a girth-5 cubic with zero (5,7)-wed
          +ge events AND zero (6,6)-wedge events, i.e., a graph whose C_8
          + production cannot come from 2-edge wedge-sharing. Such graphs
          + have c_8 вүҘ 9 in the data, so they DO have C_8s вҖ” produced via
          + either C_5+C_5 1-edge sharing or C_7+C_7 3-edge sharing, neit
          +her of which the current probe tracks.                        
      118 +                                                              
      119 +The reformulated EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE conjecture (that wedge-sha
          +ring always bridges to C_8) is therefore **falsified at growin
          +g rates with n**. At n=80, ~18% of graphs falsify it. The wedg
          +e mechanism is a partial mechanism, not a bridging conjecture.
      120 +                                                              
      121 +**Cooperative bound trend is sub-linear and tightening with sa
          +mple size:**                                                  
      122 +                                                              
      123 +```                                                           
      124 +n=14: min(c5+c6+c7)/n = 1.79                                  
      125 +n=40: 0.33-0.35                                               
      126 +n=60: 0.18-0.22                                               
      127 +n=70: 0.16                                                    
      128 +n=80: 0.11                                                    
      129 +```                                                           
      130 +                                                              
      131 +Approaches 0.1 at n=80. Linear cooperative bound (EG-K-COOP-LB
          +) is dead. Possibly О©(log n) or О©(1); insufficient data to dis
          +tinguish, but the trend is clear.                             
      132 +                                                              
      133 +**Zero-violator graphs reach 30% at n=80.** A "violator" = ver
          +tex with > 3 short cycles through it. Run 3 at n=80: 15/50 gra
          +phs (30%) have ZERO violators. The crude vertex-overflow pigeo
          +nhole argument is not just sometimes-failing but routinely-fai
          +ling at large n.                                              
      134 +                                                              
      135 +**Outlier structural signature (consistent across all three ru
          +ns):**                                                        
      136 +- Low c_5 (typically 1-2)                                     
      137 +- High c_7 (often 8-15)                                       
      138 +- Plenty of (6,7)вҶ’C_9 and (7,7)вҶ’C_10 wedge events (which produ
          +ce C_9 and C_10, not C_8)                                     
      139 +- Zero or near-zero (5,7) and (6,6) wedge events              
      140 +- Still c_8 вүҘ 9                                               
      141 +                                                              
      142 +So the cascade the paper describes (5-cycles thinning as n gro
          +ws) is the structural origin of wedge-mechanism outliers. Outl
          +iers are exactly the graphs where 5-cycles have become so spar
          +se that 5-cycle-incident wedge-sharing can no longer happen.  
      143 +                                                              
      144 +### Verdict on the conjecture                                 
      145 +                                                              
      146 +EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE in its strong form ("every girth-5 cubic pr
          +oduces C_8 via wedge-sharing") is **DEAD** вҖ” falsified at 18% 
          +rate by n=80, with rate growing in n. As a *bridging* conjectu
          +re for the open question, it fails: wedge-sharing is provably 
          +insufficient as the sole mechanism.                           
      147 +                                                              
      148 +EG-K-COOP-LB at linear scale is **DEAD** вҖ” falsified by min(c5
          ++c6+c7)/n вҶ’ 0.11.                                             
      149 +                                                              
      150 +The structural conjecture itself (every girth-5 cubic has SOME
          + XOR-constructible C_8) remains consistent with all 1024 graph
          +s (every graph has c_8 вүҘ 5). At large n, the proof must lean s
          +pecifically on C_5+C_5 1-edge and C_7+C_7 3-edge mechanisms вҖ” 
          +exactly the mechanisms the current probe doesn't track.       
      151 +                                                              
      152 +### Verdict on the protocol (v1 draft, now n=1+scaling instead
          + of just n=1)                                                 
      153 +                                                              
      154 +The protocol-as-executed produced quantitative findings that *
          +redirect* the structural-conjecture proof effort:             
      155 +1. Wedge mechanism is insufficient at growing rates with n (re
          +al, measurable, not in the paper)                             
      156 +2. Cooperative bound at linear scale dies (rules out a class o
          +f pigeonhole arguments)                                       
      157 +3. Vertex-overflow forcing dies routinely at large n (rules ou
          +t a class of crude bounds)                                    
      158 +                                                              
      159 +These are negative results, but in the WHYвҶ’HOW sense they're *
          +useful* negatives вҖ” they constrain what future bridging conjec
          +tures must look like. The proof must lean on:                 
      160 +- C_5+C_5 1-edge sharing (not 2-edge wedge sharing)           
      161 +- C_7+C_7 3-edge sharing                                      
      162 +- Some structural property that holds even when c_5 is small  
      163 +                                                              
      164 +The next pass of the protocol вҖ” should it run вҖ” would extend t
          +he probe to track all four XOR mechanisms and produce a comple
          +te mechanism-distribution map. That graduates from "test the w
          +edge bridge" to "characterize which mechanisms produce C_8 in 
          +the population." Not done in this overlook.

  Sandbox artifacts (all .prometheus/explore/, all Level 0):
  - EXPLORE-2026-04-27-knowledge-generator-eg-test.md вҖ” full pass log + scaling
  addendum

  What we accomplished and experienced:

  The 2026-03-25 knowledge-generator proposal runs but had three operational
  gaps that surfaced under load:
  1. No template for steps 1-4 вҶ’ I had to ad-lib
  2. No logical-self-check step вҶ’ I shipped a structurally flawed conjecture
  (EG-K-CASCADE-WEDGE) without catching that wedge-pigeonhole gives C_6 not C_8
  in the C_5+C_5 case
  3. No graduation to scaled empirical testing вҶ’ which would have caught the
  strong-form falsification at 18% by n=80

  The probe itself produced real, useful negative findings on the ErdЕ‘s-GyГЎrfГЎs
  sub-conjecture: wedge mechanism is dead at large n, cooperative bound at
  linear scale is dead, vertex-overflow is dead. These constrain where the proof
   of the structural conjecture must go (specifically C_5+C_5 1-edge and C_7+C_7
   3-edge mechanisms).

  Parked for next session:
  - Extend probe to track all four XOR mechanisms (~30-60 min code).
  - Use the n=80 outliers as study targets (specific structural patterns to
  characterize).
  - Run open calibration: protocol on a workload-without-scaffolding.
  - After both: graduate v1 template to a v2 patch in
  Researches/crystal-self-improvement/proposals/.

  Calling overlook done unless you want one more thing.

в—Ҹ Clean reproducibility вҖ” even with the file deleted before the rerun:

  - All per-row data identical across both runs (every graph's
  c_5/c_6/c_7/c_8/violators/wedge data matches).
  - Files differ by only 2 bytes (212295 vsВ 212293), and only in the elapsed_sec
   field (e.g., n=30 went from 4.04s to 3.07s вҖ” different system load on the
  rerun, otherwise no semantic difference).
  - SHA1 differs because of those timing bytes, but content is functionally
  identical.

  So determinism confirmed at the data level. Same SEED_BASE вҶ’ same graphs вҶ’
  same analysis вҶ’ same findings. The deletion-then-fresh-write was a good clean
  test (rules out any append/merge artifact).

  This is a real free reproducibility data point вҖ” worth one line in the EXPLORE
   log if you want to add it (rerun with deletion verified bit-identical graph
  data, byte-identical except elapsed_sec). Or skip вҖ” the analysis was already
  solid; this just removes any lingering "did the seed actually determine the
  data" question.

в—Ҹ Confirmed вҖ” 10247 lines, 202K chars, ~17 lines per graph. That's
  json.dump(..., indent=2) + the per-row dict shape (9 fields each, with
  pair_lengths as a nested dict adding a few more lines per graph). Not a
  problem; just the cost of pretty-printing.

  If you ever want a more compact form for storage or transfer, dropping the
  indent would knock it to ~5K lines (one line per row); compressing further
  with json.dumps(d, separators=(',',':')) ditches all whitespace and gets it
  down to a single very long line at ~150KB. Not needed for analysis though вҖ”
  the verbose form is fine.

  Anything else, or call it?

  Effect of the differences:

  - SAMPLES_PER_N controls target graphs per n. 30 vsВ 100. Run 1 hits
  acceptance-rate ceiling at n=14 (gets 24 instead ofВ 30); Run 2 hits target at
  all n.
  - MAX_TRIES_FACTOR is the rejection-sample budget. max_tries = SAMPLES_PER_N *
   factor. Run 1: 30Г—200 = 6000 tries cap. Run 2: 100Г—300 = 30000 tries cap.
  Higher factor in Run 2 ensures n=14 (acceptance ~0.4%) reaches its target.
  - SEED_BASE is identical вҶ’ both runs walk the same random seed sequence at
  n=14, so Run 1's 24 graphs == Run 2's first 24 graphs at n=14. For nвүҘ20 they
  diverge (Run 2 used more tries at n=14, advancing the cursor further).
  - OUTPUT_JSON just names the file.

  Run 1 paste block (already gave you this above):

  N_VALUES = [14, 20, 30, 40, 50, 60]
  SAMPLES_PER_N = 30
  MAX_TRIES_FACTOR = 200
  SEED_BASE = 12345
  OUTPUT_JSON = "eg_probe_run1.json"

  Run 2 paste block (for the file you already reran):

  N_VALUES = [14, 20, 30, 40, 50, 60]
  SAMPLES_PER_N = 100
  MAX_TRIES_FACTOR = 300
  SEED_BASE = 12345
  OUTPUT_JSON = "eg_probe_run2.json"

> Don't they look the same? LOL                                                 

в—Ҹ Yeah, basically yes. Run 2 is "Run 1 with more samples and more rejection
  budget." Same probe, same seed, same n range вҖ” the only real changes are two
  numbers tweaked.

  That's actually a feature, not a bug вҖ” the probe is parameterized cleanly
  enough that "scaling up" is literally just numbers up. No code change, no
  separate file, no new methodology. The interesting variation came from data,
  not config.

  Goes to show how much of the "Run 1 vs Run 2" distinction in my analysis was
  hindsight pretending to be design.

> Ah, samples per n is different. I see.                                        

в—Ҹ Yep вҖ” SAMPLES_PER_N is the one that actually matters. Run 1's 30 vs Run 2's
  100 is what gave the bigger sample size, the better statistics, and the
  visible outlier-rate trend. The MAX_TRIES_FACTOR bump from 200 to 300 was just
   a budget knob to make sure n=14 (low acceptance rate) could reach the new
  target вҖ” supporting cast, not the headliner.

  So one knob is doing the lifting. The other two changes are filename and "give
   it enough budget to succeed."

в—Ҹ Production-ready file at .prometheus/explore/eg_probe_v2.py. Paste this on
  your work machine (~/playground/eg_probe_v2.py or wherever fits), keep the
  venv active, run it. Default config matches Run 2 (n=14..60, 100 samples) with
   OUTPUT_JSON = "eg_probe_v2_output.json". Adjust if you want a smaller smoke
  test first or a wider sweep.

  Here's the contents to copy:

  """Extended probe -- tracks ALL FOUR XOR mechanisms producing C_8 in girth-5
  cubic graphs. Iteration 2 of the v1 knowledge-generator protocol on the
  Erdos-Gyarfas workload.

  XOR mechanisms (paper's Theorem 3.4):
    C_5 + C_5 sharing 1 edge   -> C_8
    C_5 + C_7 sharing 2 edges  -> C_8
    C_6 + C_6 sharing 2 edges  -> C_8
    C_7 + C_7 sharing 3 edges  -> C_8

  For 2- and 3-edge sharing, the shared edges must form a path (connected,
  2 deg-1 vertices, rest deg-2) for the XOR to yield a single simple cycle.

  Sandbox artifact. Not promoted, not gate-passed.
  """

  import json
  import random
  import time
  from collections import Counter, defaultdict
  from itertools import combinations

  import networkx as nx


  N_VALUES = [14, 20, 30, 40, 50, 60]
  SAMPLES_PER_N = 100
  MAX_TRIES_FACTOR = 300
  SEED_BASE = 12345
  OUTPUT_JSON = "eg_probe_v2_output.json"


  def true_girth(G):
      best = float("inf")
      for src in G.nodes():
          dist = {src: 0}
          parent = {src: None}
          queue = [src]
          local_best = float("inf")
          while queue:
              new_queue = []
              for u in queue:
                  for v in G.neighbors(u):
                      if v not in dist:
                          dist[v] = dist[u] + 1
                          parent[v] = u
                          new_queue.append(v)
                      elif parent[u] != v:
                          cyc = dist[u] + dist[v] + 1
                          if cyc < local_best:
                              local_best = cyc
              queue = new_queue
          if local_best < best:
              best = local_best
          if best == 3:
              break
      return best


  def enum_cycles_by_length(G, max_len):
      by_len = defaultdict(list)
      seen = set()
      for cyc in nx.simple_cycles(G, length_bound=max_len):
          L = len(cyc)
          if L < 3:
              continue
          key = frozenset(frozenset((cyc[i], cyc[(i + 1) % L])) for i in
  range(L))
          if key in seen:
              continue
          seen.add(key)
          by_len[L].append((tuple(cyc), key))
      return by_len


  def is_path(edges):
      if not edges:
          return False
      if len(edges) == 1:
          return True
      deg = Counter()
      for e in edges:
          for v in e:
              deg[v] += 1
      leaves = sum(1 for d in deg.values() if d == 1)
      interior = sum(1 for d in deg.values() if d == 2)
      if leaves != 2 or interior != len(deg) - 2:
          return False
      leaf = next(v for v, d in deg.items() if d == 1)
      visited = {leaf}
      queue = [leaf]
      while queue:
          new_queue = []
          for u in queue:
              for e in edges:
                  if u in e:
                      other = next(v for v in e if v != u)
                      if other not in visited:
                          visited.add(other)
                          new_queue.append(other)
          queue = new_queue
      return len(visited) == len(deg)


  def count_xor_c8_mechanisms(cycles_by_len):
      mech_counts = Counter()
      candidate_targets = {
          (5, 5): 1,
          (5, 7): 2,
          (6, 6): 2,
          (7, 7): 3,
      }
      for (a, b), k in candidate_targets.items():
          cyc_a_list = cycles_by_len.get(a, [])
          cyc_b_list = cycles_by_len.get(b, [])
          if a == b:
              for (_, ea), (_, eb) in combinations(cyc_a_list, 2):
                  shared = ea & eb
                  if len(shared) == k and is_path(shared):
                      mech_counts[(a, b, k)] += 1
          else:
              for (_, ea) in cyc_a_list:
                  for (_, eb) in cyc_b_list:
                      shared = ea & eb
                      if len(shared) == k and is_path(shared):
                          mech_counts[(a, b, k)] += 1
      return mech_counts


  def per_vertex_cycle_counts(cycles_by_len, lengths=(5, 6, 7)):
      out = defaultdict(Counter)
      for L in lengths:
          for cyc_tuple, _ in cycles_by_len.get(L, []):
              for v in cyc_tuple:
                  out[v][L] += 1
      return out


  def analyze_graph(G):
      cycles = enum_cycles_by_length(G, 8)
      c5 = len(cycles.get(5, []))
      c6 = len(cycles.get(6, []))
      c7 = len(cycles.get(7, []))
      c8 = len(cycles.get(8, []))
      pv = per_vertex_cycle_counts(cycles, lengths=(5, 6, 7))
      max_cycles_per_v = 0
      violator_count = 0
      for v, counter in pv.items():
          total_at_v = counter[5] + counter[6] + counter[7]
          if total_at_v > max_cycles_per_v:
              max_cycles_per_v = total_at_v
          if total_at_v > 3:
              violator_count += 1
      mech = count_xor_c8_mechanisms(cycles)
      c5c5_1 = mech.get((5, 5, 1), 0)
      c5c7_2 = mech.get((5, 7, 2), 0)
      c6c6_2 = mech.get((6, 6, 2), 0)
      c7c7_3 = mech.get((7, 7, 3), 0)
      coverage = sum(1 for x in (c5c5_1, c5c7_2, c6c6_2, c7c7_3) if x > 0)
      return {
          "c5": c5, "c6": c6, "c7": c7, "c8": c8,
          "sum_5_6_7": c5 + c6 + c7,
          "max_cycles_per_v": max_cycles_per_v,
          "violators": violator_count,
          "c5c5_1edge_c8": c5c5_1,
          "c5c7_2edge_c8": c5c7_2,
          "c6c6_2edge_c8": c6c6_2,
          "c7c7_3edge_c8": c7c7_3,
          "mechanism_coverage": coverage,
          "total_xor_c8_events": c5c5_1 + c5c7_2 + c6c6_2 + c7c7_3,
      }


  def sample_girth5_cubics(n, target, max_tries, seed_start):
      out = []
      tries = 0
      s = seed_start
      while len(out) < target and tries < max_tries:
          tries += 1
          s += 1
          random.seed(s)
          try:
              G = nx.random_regular_graph(3, n, seed=s)
          except nx.NetworkXError:
              continue
          if not nx.is_connected(G):
              continue
          if true_girth(G) == 5:
              out.append(G)
      return out, tries


  def main():
      print("=" * 72)
      print("Extended probe v2 -- ALL 4 XOR mechanisms tracked")
      print(f"n in {N_VALUES}, target {SAMPLES_PER_N} graphs per n")
      print("=" * 72)
      all_results = {}
      seed_cursor = SEED_BASE
      for n in N_VALUES:
          t0 = time.time()
          max_tries = SAMPLES_PER_N * MAX_TRIES_FACTOR
          print(f"\n--- n={n} ---")
          graphs, tries = sample_girth5_cubics(n, SAMPLES_PER_N, max_tries,
  seed_cursor)
          seed_cursor += tries
          print(f"  sampled {len(graphs)}/{SAMPLES_PER_N} ({tries} tries, "
                f"acceptance ~{len(graphs)/tries:.1%})")
          if not graphs:
              print("  no girth-5 cubics found; skipping n")
              continue
          rows = []
          for i, G in enumerate(graphs):
              r = analyze_graph(G)
              rows.append(r)
              if (i + 1) % 10 == 0:
                  print(f"    analyzed {i+1}/{len(graphs)} ...")
          c8s = [r["c8"] for r in rows]
          cov = [r["mechanism_coverage"] for r in rows]
          zero_cov = sum(1 for c in cov if c == 0)
          no_c8 = sum(1 for r in rows if r["c8"] == 0)
          c5c5 = sum(r["c5c5_1edge_c8"] for r in rows)
          c5c7 = sum(r["c5c7_2edge_c8"] for r in rows)
          c6c6 = sum(r["c6c6_2edge_c8"] for r in rows)
          c7c7 = sum(r["c7c7_3edge_c8"] for r in rows)
          graphs_with_c5c5 = sum(1 for r in rows if r["c5c5_1edge_c8"] > 0)
          graphs_with_c5c7 = sum(1 for r in rows if r["c5c7_2edge_c8"] > 0)
          graphs_with_c6c6 = sum(1 for r in rows if r["c6c6_2edge_c8"] > 0)
          graphs_with_c7c7 = sum(1 for r in rows if r["c7c7_3edge_c8"] > 0)
          elapsed = time.time() - t0
          ng = len(rows)
          print(f"  c_8: min={min(c8s)} mean={sum(c8s)/ng:.1f} max={max(c8s)}
  #zero_c8={no_c8}")
          print(f"  mechanism coverage (out of 4): "
                f"min={min(cov)} mean={sum(cov)/ng:.2f} max={max(cov)}
  #zero_cov={zero_cov}")
          print(f"  graphs with mechanism present:")
          print(f"    C5+C5 1-edge: {graphs_with_c5c5}/{ng}
  ({100*graphs_with_c5c5/ng:.0f}%)")
          print(f"    C5+C7 2-edge: {graphs_with_c5c7}/{ng}
  ({100*graphs_with_c5c7/ng:.0f}%)")
          print(f"    C6+C6 2-edge: {graphs_with_c6c6}/{ng}
  ({100*graphs_with_c6c6/ng:.0f}%)")
          print(f"    C7+C7 3-edge: {graphs_with_c7c7}/{ng}
  ({100*graphs_with_c7c7/ng:.0f}%)")
          print(f"  total events across graphs: "
                f"C5+C5={c5c5} C5+C7={c5c7} C6+C6={c6c6} C7+C7={c7c7}")
          print(f"  elapsed: {elapsed:.2f}s")
          all_results[n] = {
              "n_graphs": len(graphs),
              "tries": tries,
              "elapsed_sec": elapsed,
              "rows": rows,
          }
      with open(OUTPUT_JSON, "w") as f:
          json.dump(all_results, f, indent=2)
      print(f"\nSaved results to {OUTPUT_JSON}")


  if __name__ == "__main__":
      main()

   вҖ” meaning they have C_8s but my probe reports none of the 4 XOR mechanisms

  3.6) вҖ” would mean those C_8s are not XOR-decomposable from short-cycle pairs.
  Major finding.

  STEP 4 вҖ” Logical self-check fires HARD. Before drafting a conjecture from
  this:

  The implication chain "2/600 graphs falsify the structural conjecture" rests
  on the assumption my probe is correct. Most likely explanation for these
  outliers is probe bug, not counterexample. The paper sampled 1026 graphs and
  found zero counterexamples; my 600 sample contains 2. Bayesian smell: bug is
  more likely than a 0.3% counterexample rate the paper missed.

  Step 4 verdict on this candidate: FLAGGED вҖ” verify probe before claiming.
  Concrete checks:

  1. Run probe on Petersen graph (n=10, paper's reference case). Petersen has
  c_5=12, c_8=15, all C_8s XOR-constructible via C_5+C_5. If probe reports
  anything other than mechanism_coverage=4 with C_5+C_5 events, probe is wrong.
  2. Manually inspect the two outlier graphs. Extract n=40 row 97 (c5=4, c6=7,
  c7=8, c8=10), enumerate cycle pairs by hand or with a second-implementation
  tool, see if any actually IS a valid XOR mechanism the probe missed.
  3. Check is_path edge cases. The path-connectedness check might be too strict
  for some legitimate cases.

  Until verification: the n=40/n=60 outlier finding does NOT propagate to Step 
  5.

  The other 4 patterns (mechanism cascade across n, C_5+C_5 declining 91%вҶ’35%,
  C_7+C_7 roughly stable, mean_coverage falling 3.91вҶ’2.38) are robust regardless
   of the probe-bug question вҖ” they don't depend on the zero-coverage edge
  cases.

  Want me to run the Petersen sanity check now? That's the single cheapest
  verification step.

> What does this mean in terms of the knowledge generator and the WHY/HOW what  
  we're doing actually?                                                         

в—Ҹ Good question вҖ” let me reflect on it with the framework rather than just
  narrating.

  What just happened operationally. I drafted a candidate conjecture from V2
  data ("2/600 graphs falsify the structural conjecture"). Step 4 (logical
  self-check) fired and downgraded it from VERIFIED to FLAGGED вҖ” pointing at
  unverified probe correctness as the load-bearing premise. The protocol
  prevented me from running Step 5 (falsification) on a possibly-corrupted
  basis.

  This is iteration 2 catching a DIFFERENT failure mode than iteration 1:

  - Iteration 1 catch: structural flaw IN the implication chain вҖ”
  wedge-pigeonhole gives C_6 not C_8 (a math error).
  - Iteration 2 catch: unverified premise feeding the chain вҖ” probe might be
  buggy (a data-collection error).

  Same gate (Step 4), different fault classes. Both are "candidate conjecture
  isn't ready for falsification, and here's why specifically." The gate is more
  general than how I named it in the v1 draft вҖ” it's not just "trace the
  implication chain to the open question," it's "verify all load-bearing
  premises before falsification, including the premise that your data is
  correctly measured."

  WHY=HOW analysis on Step 4 itself:

  - WHY Step 4 exists: substrate confirmation bias вҖ” when the LLM produces a
  conjecture, the LLM doesn't auto-flag flaws in its own output.
  - HOW Step 4 works: explicit pre-falsification verification of all premises.
  - Conjugate? Yes. The HOW only matters because the WHY is real (substrate
  bias). The WHY only matters because no other gate catches it (FRAME surfaces
  implicit conditions but doesn't trace claim-to-data; BLIND-VERIFY runs after
  the conjecture is fully formed; PARALLAX is multi-lens but not
  premise-by-premise).
  - WHYвҮҢHOW verdict: STRUCTURAL. Step 4 can't be removed without re-opening the
  substrate-bias hole. It's not a convenient patch for the knowledge-generator
  protocol specifically вҖ” it's a generic add-on to any conjecture-engine. That's
   a stronger architectural claim than I had after iterationВ 1.

  Architecturally what this means for the v1 draft graduation:

  - n=2 evidence base now exists for the v1 protocol with Step 4 вҖ” and the two
  trials caught two different fault classes, which is better than two trials
  catching the same class. Diverse catches indicate the gate is general.
  - Step 4's scope refinement is also part of the n=2 finding. v1 draft said
  "trace implication chain"; iteration 2 shows it should also cover "verify
  data-collection premise." That's a v1.1 patch to the v1 draft itself, surfaced
   by the protocol-running-on-itself.
  - Positive externality firing in real time. Step 4 didn't just block me вҖ” it
  generated a non-obvious next move (run Petersen sanity check). The constraint
  produced a creative direction instead of just "no, stop." That's the
  gate-stack design intent from CRYSTAL.md.

  What "we're actually doing" right now:

  We're validating that the v1 protocol is robust against its own builder's
  confirmation bias вҖ” using the protocol itself as the validator, on a workload
  where confirmation bias would be costly (claiming a counterexample to a
  published conjecture). The protocol stopped me. That's the load-bearing test.

  The Petersen sanity check I proposed isn't just "verify the probe" вҖ” it's the
  natural Step 4 output on this candidate. The protocol is running cleanly.

  Whether the outliers turn out to be real counterexamples or probe bugs is now
  secondary to the architectural finding: Step 4 has earned its place via two 
  different fault catches, the gate is structural by WHYвҮҢHOW, and the v1 draft 
  is genuinely closer to graduation-ready.

вң» SautГ©ed for 52s

> What does the n=2 evidence mean for us? this sounds like a huge step for me   
  (compared to where we started from) almost like in the millenium problems     
  getting from rank 1 to 2 in some areas. Is it really that relevant?           

в—Ҹ Honest calibration: the comparison to rank-1вҶ’2 in MP work is overstating it.
  Let me be specific about what n=2 here actually does and doesn't mean.

  What n=2 here actually means (modestly):
  - The v1 protocol has been run twice
  - Step 4 fired usefully on two different fault classes (math-flaw, then
  data-correctness-flaw)
  - Two data points = "this isn't a one-off success"

  What n=2 here does NOT mean:
  - Both trials were on the same workload (ErdЕ‘s-GyГЎrfГЎs girth-5 cubics). It's
  n=1 workload tested twice, not n=2 different workloads.
  - Both trials were same-instance, same-session, same substrate. By
  feedback_arxiv_readiness.md's "вүҘ2 independent artifacts" rule, this is
  provisional evidence at best вҖ” same-instance trials don't satisfy the
  cross-substrate independence the rule demands.
  - The 2026-03-25 proposal's prescribed open calibration
  (workload-without-scaffolding) is still completely undone. That's a known,
  named gap.
  - No external validation (other LLM, other instance, human reviewer) has
  touched this.

  Why the rank-1вҶ’2 MP analogy doesn't fit:

  Rank-1вҶ’2 in MP work is a mathematical structural advance вҖ” a proof that
  establishes harder structural behavior. It's the difference between "trivial
  case works" and "genuinely-hard case works under proof." The BSD Formal Group
  Floor going from rank-1 to rank-2 was a real theorem.

  n=2 trials of an empirical protocol is a small-sample empirical signal. It's
  the difference between "we tried it once" and "we tried it twice on the same
  problem." Different category of progress entirely.

  What it IS, properly scoped:

  It's a non-trivial incremental forward step in protocol development вҖ” moving
  from "n=1 trial caught a math-flaw" to "n=2 trials caught two different fault
  classes, which suggests the gate generalizes within this workload." That's a
  real step, but it's a step in capability development, not in mathematical
  advancement.

  Where the protocol actually stands:

  - v1 draft is closer to graduation-ready than after iteration 1 alone
  - Still NOT graduation-ready: needs the open calibration + at least one
  external review + ideally a cross-workload trial
  - Per feedback_dont_promote_mid_arc.md, n=2 same-workload same-instance does
  not warrant promoting the v1 draft to a v2 patch in Researches/

  Reality check on excitement:

  I named two real findings cleanly (Step 4 caught two fault classes; WHYвҮҢHOW
  analysis suggests Step 4 is structural not convenient). Those findings are
  defensible. But framing them as "huge step" is on me reading more into the
  evidence than it carries. The architectural claim is correct in shape; the
  scale is small.

  So: a real but modest step forward in protocol development. Not analogous to
  rank-1вҶ’2 advances in mathematical work. The right honest framing is "we have
  evidence the gate works; we don't yet have evidence it generalizes."

> If they come from longer-cycle XORs is that a good sign but also meaning it's 
   more complex? Also maybe complex in knowledge generation or do we not know   
  we only now assumingly the paths are more complex and not more?               

в—Ҹ Both. Real both. Let me decompose because they're separable questions.

  Good sign vs. complexity sign:

  If the outlier C_8s ARE explainable via longer-cycle XORs (e.g., C_5+C_9
  sharing 3 edges, C_6+C_8 sharing 3, etc.):
  - Good: the proof strategy is salvageable вҖ” Conj 3.6 just needs to extend the
  cycle range from {5,6,7} to {5..K} for some K. The main conjecture (every
  girth-5 cubic has C_8) survives via a broader mechanism family. The bridge
  from "structural" to "main" still works.
  - Complex: more cycle-pair families to enumerate. The paper's clean
  4-mechanism enumeration becomes 8 or 12 or N mechanisms. Each new family needs
   its own path-connectedness analysis, its own conditions. The simpler version
  was preferred because it was clean; the broader version is messier to prove.

  So yes вҖ” it would be a good sign that "the strategy works at all," and a
  complexity sign that "the cleanest version doesn't hold."

  Two flavors of complexity, separable:

  1. Knowledge-generation complexity (how hard for us to find/check these):
  SMALL. Extending the probe to longer cycles is mechanical вҖ” same enumeration
  logic, wider cycle range. ~10 lines of code, maybe 2-3x slower runtime. The
  probe doesn't get qualitatively harder.
  2. Mathematical complexity (how hard the underlying math becomes): UNKNOWN.
  Three possibilities, no way to distinguish without testing:
    - Bounded extension: the outliers all decompose via a small finite set of
  additional families (say 4-8 more mechanisms). "More cases, same shape, still
  tractable."
    - Unbounded family: needing arbitrarily long cycles, infinite-case proof.
  "Different problem entirely."
    - Some outliers don't decompose via any cycle pair at all: the XOR strategy
  is incomplete, not just incompletely-stated. C_8s in those graphs come from
  non-XOR construction, and the structural proof approach fundamentally doesn't
  reach them.

  Your instinct that we "only assumingly" know the paths are more complex is 
  correct.

  We don't know which of the three above holds. We're assuming the first
  (bounded extension) is most likely because it's the natural extension of the
  paper's framework вҖ” but we haven't tested. If we extended the probe to length
  12 or 14 cycles and ran it on the two outliers, we'd find out. Three outcomes:
  - Outliers decompose вҶ’ option 1 (bounded extension), structural strategy
  salvageable
  - Outliers decompose only via very long cycles вҶ’ option 2 (unbounded),
  strategy needs new ideas
  - Outliers still don't decompose even at long cycles вҶ’ option 3 (XOR strategy
  incomplete), main conjecture provable but structural proof needs different
  approach

  Each outcome is informative. The cheapest test (extend probe to length 9 or
  10, run on the two extracted graphs) would distinguish them in maybe 15
  minutes of code + a minute of compute.

  To your question's deeper shape: complexity in knowledge generation (probe
  extension) is cheap. Complexity in the underlying mathematics is what we'd
  discover, not what we'd add. The protocol's job here would be to find out
  which complexity regime we're actually in вҖ” and Step 4 would still apply
  (don't claim "bounded extension" without verifying, etc.).

  Want me to extend the probe to test, or call it iteration-2 done with this
  open question parked clearly?

  Real findings:
  - All 600 graphs covered by K вүӨ 11 in our sample. Bounded, modestly growing
  with n.
