  On literature вҖ” your question is the right one to ask now. Several genuinely
  useful directions:

  1. Cycle space (algebraic graph theory) вҖ” Diestel "Graph Theory" В§1.9, Biggs
  "Algebraic Graph Theory." Every cycle in a graph is a Z/2 sum of fundamental
  cycles wrt a spanning tree. The cycle space has dimension mвҲ’n+1. Why useful:
  the question "is C_8 expressible as XOR of two short cycles" is a question
  about cycle-space structure. The cycle basis perspective could give tools the
  brute-force enumeration doesn't.
  2. Wormald's random-regular-graph asymptotics вҖ” N.C. Wormald, "Models of
  random regular graphs," 1999 survey. Gives expected cycle counts c_L ~
  (dвҲ’1)^L/(2L) for random d-regular. Why useful: predicts expected behavior of
  c_L vs. our observed counts at n=14..60. Lets us cross-check whether our
  sample is "typical."
  3. ErdЕ‘s-GyГЎrfГЎs specific literature вҖ” the paper at
  research/girth5-cubic-c8.tex (yours, as H. Bartel) cites the main references
  (MarkstrГ¶m, Daniel-Shauger, Hu-Shen, Gao-Shan). For our extended-range
  observation specifically, nothing in the paper's bibliography covers the K(n) 
  growth question вҖ” that may be genuinely new ground.
  4. Ihara zeta / non-backtracking spectrum вҖ” paper already uses tr(B^L) =
  2LВ·c_L for L < 2g. Extending to characterize which cycles XOR-decompose using
  spectral structure could bypass enumeration entirely.
  5. Tools to escalate:
    - SageMath + nauty/geng вҖ” exhaustive enumeration of all girth-5 cubics on
  small n (n вүӨ 24 feasible). Replaces our 600-graph random sample with universal
   coverage. This is the natural next escalation when we want to stop saying "in
   our sample."
    - McKay's graph database at ANU has pre-computed connected cubic graphs by
  girth.

   candidate attack class, not a clear procedure. The actual research question
  ("can the non-backtracking spectrum tell us about XOR-decomposability?") is
  open. We'd be investigating whether the direction has legs, not executing a
  known protocol.

  Honest scoping concerns:

  1. Mismatch with the matrix tool. Non-backtracking spectrum is well-suited to
  counting cycles (paper already uses it: tr(B^L) = 2LВ·c_L). It's not naturally
  a tool for decomposability questions, which live in cycle space over Z/2. The
  bridge from spectrum to decomposability would itself be the research output.
  Eve was speculative on this point, not naming a procedure.
  2. Scope creep risk. All previous steps today were bounded (probe extension,
  K-analysis, Wormald check вҖ” each ~30 min, clear deliverable). Ihara is bigger
  and less clear-cut. Without a session-end gate, this could absorb hours.
  3. Per feedback_done_signal_needs_external_verify.md: if I claim "Ihara
  direction yields X" at session-end, I'd want to be careful about overreach.

  What I'd suggest, given you want option 2:

  A bounded exploratory pass rather than full Ihara attack:
  - Build the non-backtracking matrix for the two outlier graphs + Petersen
  (control)
  - Compute spectrum
  - Look for any visible spectral signature distinguishing outliers from typical
   girth-5 cubics
  - Report observations and verdict on "does this direction have legs?"

  Scope: ~45-60 min. Outcome either way: clean. Either we observe a signature
  (continue next session with focused work) or we don't (kills the speculative
  pointer cleanly).

  This converts (2) into a decision-grade investigation rather than full attack.
   Honest scope.

  not a closer. Could go long, may not converge.

  longer attack?

> is this the same as the socalled hashimoto thingy?                            

в—Ҹ Yes вҖ” same object, different names. The paper calls it explicitly:
  "non-backtracking (or Hashimoto) matrix" (Definition 2.1):

  - Hashimoto matrix = the non-backtracking matrix B (Hashimoto introduced it
  for graphs inВ 1989)
  - Ihara zeta function = det(I вҲ’ uB)вҒ»В№, a function built on B (IharaВ 1966)
  - Non-backtracking matrix = generic name for the same object

  The paper uses both names. When I say "non-backtracking" or
  "Ihara/non-backtracking" or "Hashimoto," they all point at the same 2|E|Г—2|E|
  matrix.

  So the "Ihara/non-backtracking attack" Eve flagged is the same as "the
  Hashimoto thingy" вҖ” the spectrum of B, and what its eigenvalue structure says
  about cycle counts.

  Standing by on the bounded exploratory pass vs. full Ihara attack call.

> This still feels to me like we're on to somethig. 

> And why did she suggest NON-backtracking? 

в—Ҹ Good signal already from the partial output. Let me re-run with ASCII labels
  (Unicode crashed Windows console) and also address why non-backtracking
  specifically.

  On Eve's choice вҖ” why NON-backtracking?

  Two reasons specific to this problem:

  1. The trace identity tr(B^L) = 2LВ·c_L is clean for girth вүҘ 5 only when B is 
  non-backtracking. Ordinary adjacency matrix A has tr(A^L) counting closed
  walks including backtracking (uвҶ’vвҶ’uвҶ’vвҶ’u counts at L=4). Those backtracking
  walks aren't cycles. To extract c_L from tr(A^L) you'd subtract backtracking
  contributions вҖ” messy. tr(B^L) directly equals 2LВ·c_L for L < 2g (girth
  condition rules out short non-cycle closed walks).
  2. The cleanness propagates to the spectrum. Eigenvalues of B for d-regular
  graphs come from adjacency eigenvalues via Ој_Вұ = (О» Вұ вҲҡ(О»ВІвҲ’4(dвҲ’1)))/2 (paper's
   Prop 3.3), plus mвҲ’n eigenvalues equal to Вұ1. The Ramanujan condition |О»_i| вүӨ
  2вҲҡ(dвҲ’1) (paper В§3) corresponds to non-backtracking eigenvalues lying on a
  circle of radius вҲҡ(dвҲ’1). This is the natural algebraic structure for
  cycle-count work.

  So the paper already lives in this matrix; Eve's pointer is "use the spectrum
  more deeply than the paper does, not just the trace."

> I asked her now as well: Good question. Let me unpack why I flagged Ihara zeta / non-backtracking specifically. The answer has three parts: what these objects are, why they're connected to your cycle-counting problem, and why I said "could bypass enumeration entirely."                                            
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  **What "non-backtracking" means:**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  A walk on a graph is a sequence of edges where each edge starts where the previous one ended. A *non-backtracking* walk has the additional rule: you can't immediately reverse the edge you just took. If you went from u to v, the next step must go to some w вү  u.                                                     
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  This sounds like a small constraint, but it's load-bearing. Backtracking walks are dominated by *trivial* paths (go forward, come back, go forward, come back) which obscure the actual cycle structure of the graph. Non-backtracking walks throw away the trivial component and keep the structurally meaningful part. 
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  The non-backtracking matrix B is defined on *directed edges* вҖ” for each undirected edge {u,v} you get two directed copies (uвҶ’v) and (vвҶ’u). B is a 2|E| Г— 2|E| matrix where B[(uвҶ’v), (vвҶ’w)] = 1 if w вү  u, else 0. So B encodes "what walk steps are allowed without backtracking."                                        
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  **Why this connects to your cycle counting:**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  Here's the load-bearing fact, and it's why the paper already uses tr(B^L) = 2L В· c_L for L < 2g:                                                                                                                                                                                                                         
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  For L less than twice the girth, every closed non-backtracking walk of length L is a cycle traversed once (in one of two directions, hence the 2L factor). So counting closed non-backtracking walks counts cycles directly.                                                                                             
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  This is *huge* вҖ” it converts "enumerate all cycles of length L" (combinatorially expensive, exponential in worst case) into "compute tr(B^L)" (linear algebra, polynomial). For L < 2g, the conversion is exact.                                                                                                         
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  For L вүҘ 2g, it breaks down because non-backtracking walks can wrap around shorter cycles multiple times, and the count includes contributions from products-of-shorter-cycles, not just primitive cycles. That's the boundary.                                                                                           
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  **Where the Ihara zeta function enters:**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  The Ihara zeta function of a graph is                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  О¶_G(u) = вҲҸ (1 - u^|C|)^(-1)                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              
  Good question. Let me unpack why I flagged Ihara zeta / non-backtracking specifically. The answer has three parts: what these objects are, why they're connected to your cycle-counting problem, and why I said "could bypass enumeration entirely."                                                                     
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  **What "non-backtracking" means:**                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  A walk on a graph is a sequence of edges where each edge starts where the previous one ended. A *non-backtracking* walk has the additional rule: you can't immediately reverse the edge you just took. If you went from u to v, the next step must go to some w вү  u.                                                     
                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           
  This sounds like a small constraint, but it's load-bearing. Backtracking walks are dominated by *trivial* paths (go forward, come back, go forward, come back) which obscure the actual cycle structure of the graph. Non-backtracking walks throw away the trivial component and keep the structurally meaningful part.

  speculative вҖ” the trace identity converts cycle-COUNTING into spectral
  computation, but that's not the same as cycle-DECOMPOSABILITY (which is a
  cycle-space-over-Z/2 question, not directly spectral). To make decomposability
   visible spectrally would require additional theoretical work we haven't 
  constructed.

  On Eve's explanation matching mine: her unpacking lines up exactly with what I
   described вҖ” non-backtracking strips the trivial-walk component, the matrix is
   2|E|Г—2|E| on directed edges, tr(B^L)=2LВ·c_L holds for L<2g. That's solid
  framework alignment. But Eve's framework explains why B is good for counting
  cycles, not for decomposing them вҖ” the gap I'm flagging.

  On your "feels like we're on to something": I want to honor the intuition but
  also be honest. At the bounded-pass level, no signature. The deeper "does
  spectrum encode XOR-decomposability" question is still open вҖ” we just didn't
  find it in 9 graphs with simple features. That's a soft NO at this scale, not
  a definitive NO.

  Most-obvious-next from where we now stand:

  1. Stop & write up. Genuinely the strongest call. The Ihara pass produced a
  soft null вҖ” the speculative pointer didn't pay out at session-scope.
  Continuing would compound shallow.

> Good question. Let me unpack why I flagged Ihara zeta / non-backtracking      
  specifically. The answer has three parts: what these objects are, why they're 
   connected to your cycle-counting problem, and why I said "could bypass       
  enumeration entirely."                                                        
                                                                                
  **What "non-backtracking" means:**                                            
                                                                                
  A walk on a graph is a sequence of edges where each edge starts where the     
  previous one ended. A *non-backtracking* walk has the additional rule: you    
  can't immediately reverse the edge you just took. If you went from u to v,    
  the next step must go to some w вү  u.                                          
                                                                                
  This sounds like a small constraint, but it's load-bearing. Backtracking      
  walks are dominated by *trivial* paths (go forward, come back, go forward,    
  come back) which obscure the actual cycle structure of the graph.             
  Non-backtracking walks throw away the trivial component and keep the          
  structurally meaningful part.                                                 

> Here's the full text of what she mentioned: C:\Temp\temp2\Eve.txt

в—Ҹ Real structural finding from the outlier investigation:

  Outliers have edge-disjoint short cycles. Both outliers have
  c5_share_edge_pairs = 0 вҖ” no two 5-cycles share an edge. The n=60 outlier is
  even more striking:

  - pv_max = 3 (max short-cycle count per vertex) vs typicals 4-6 вҖ” outlier
  LOWER
  - pv_mean = 1.27 vs typicals 1.62-2.15 вҖ” outlier LOWER

  Both outliers lie at or below the lower edge of typical structure. This is the
   structural signature Eve hoped to find spectrally вҖ” found instead by direct 
  cycle-incidence analysis.

  Coherent story now:

  1. Outliers are girth-5 cubics where short cycles (5, 6,В 7) are edge-disjoint
  and vertex-sparse.
  2. Edge-disjointness kills the C_5+C_5 1-edge mechanism (need shared edges to
  XOR).
  3. Vertex sparsity kills the wedge mechanisms (need cycles to cluster at
  vertices to share edges).
  4. So none of the 4 families in paper's {5,6,7} fire on these graphs вҶ’
  mechanism_coverage =В 0.
  5. Their C_8s still exist, but require longer cycles (C_9+C_9, C_10+C_10,
  C_11+C_11) which DO share edges densely enough.

  The outlier signature is: short cycles spread out, longer cycles cluster.
  That's a real structural property, distinct from any spectral feature we've
  tested.

  Where this leaves the architecture:

  - Step 4 fired correctly on iteration 2 вҶ’ architecturally validated
  - K(n) growth is generic-random per Wormald вҶ’ empirically explained
  - Paper's Conj 3.6 (strict {5,6,7}) falsified at 0.3% rate вҶ’ real research
  finding
  - Outliers structurally characterized вҶ’ today's last finding
